<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: center;" align="center"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Brahman â€“ The Self</b></span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: center;" align="center"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Divine Life Society Publication: Mantras 4-8: Kenopanishad â€“ </b><a href="http://www.swami-krishnananda.org/essay/essay_2.html"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Essays on the Upanishads</b></a><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"> by Swami Krishnananda</b></span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">Brahman should be known to be other than what can be expressed by speech, thought of by the mind, seen by the eyes, heard by the ears, or revealed by lifeâ€™s functions. The nature of Truth can be known through denials alone. </span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">We cannot call Brahman <i>sat</i>, because it is the opposite of <i>asat</i>. It cannot be called <i>asat,</i> because it is the opposite of <i>sat</i>. It cannot be called <i>sadasat</i>, i.e., a combination of <i>sat</i> and <i>asat</i>, because this becomes self-contradictory. It cannot be said to be beyond <i>sat</i> and <i>asat</i>, because this is unintelligible. Thus we are cornered in every way, and all definitions of Brahman become impossible. The only way of ascertaining it is, therefore, to deny everything that we know through the senses or through the mind. </span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">Brahman is sometimes called in the Upanishads <i>asat</i> or non-existence, because the seers of the Upanishads wanted to make it clear that Brahman is nothing that exists according to our conceptions of existence. Brahman is also called many times <i>asamprajnata</i> or the unconscious or the unknown, because it is nothing that is known to us, and it is not knowledge as we understand knowledge to be. It is therefore called super-being or transcendental being, super-consciousness or transcendental consciousness. It is called <i>sat</i> or Being because the world is <i>asat</i> or non-being or perishable. It is called <i>chit</i> or consciousness because the world is <i>achit</i>, <i>jada</i> or unconsciousness. It is called <i>ananda</i> because the world is Duhkha or sorrow. It is called great because everything else is small. Thus, every characteristic which we attribute to the Divine Being is the opposite of what we experience here. But we cannot know exactly what the Divine Being is as it is in itself. </span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">Our knowledge of the perfected condition is the result of a logical deduction from our imperfect experiences. Its experience is admitted because nothing can be accounted for without such an admission. It is the one factor that gives meaning to life and explains our thoughts and behaviours, speeches and actions. Brahman, therefore, should not be mistaken to be anything that is experienced by any individual in any of its conditions. </span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">The experience of Brahman means the destruction of individuality. The expressions of individuality are always partitioned into the knower and the known. </span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"><a name="_GoBack"></a>The <i>upasana</i> (devoted worship) of a personal Divinity, no doubt, integrates the mental consciousness, collects its rays, makes it one whole being, raises the individual above the pains of the world. But it is not the same as <i>brahma-sakshatkara</i> (realisation of Brahman), because, in <i>upasana</i>, duality is not destroyed. Every object of <i>upasana</i> is based on <i>purusha</i>-<i>tantra</i>; the nature of the object of <i>upasana</i> depends upon the desire of the <i>upasaka</i>. The objects of <i>upasana</i>, therefore, differ from one person to another; but Brahman cannot differ like that. Brahman is vastu-<i>tantra</i>. Its knowledge is unshaken and dependent on nothing. It is the grand, immobile Self-existence. <i>Upasanas</i> are, therefore, helps, means, to the knowledge of Brahman. But the object of <i>upasana</i> is not Brahman.</span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">The nature of the object of <i>upasana</i> is not characterised by pure consciousness, but it is defined by the devout thought of the <i>upasaka</i>. Truth, as it is in itself, is, <i>chinmatra-svarupa</i> (of the nature of pure consciousness alone), not defined by thought. The word Brahman is derived from the root <i>brimh</i>, which means to swell, to grow great, to pervade all space, to be complete and perfect. All qualities that we attribute to Brahman are the effects of our devotion. Even the best qualities super-imposed on Brahman are what we consider as the best. The realisation of the Absolute means the renunciation of all our ideas, good or bad, great or low. It is to rest simple and silent, calm and undisturbed, in the state of wanting nothing. It is to be nothing at all, in the strictest sense. Supreme attainment is the result of supreme renunciation. When we, as persons, become non-existent, we are said to exist as Supreme Existence.</span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;">Conceptions, perceptions and forms of experience given rise to by personal interests cannot have ultimate value. Perfect and disinterested existence means the renunciation of all particularised forms of experience. It is not possible to bring down the Self to the level of what it is not and what is less than it. Knowledge, desire and action connected with the human being are guided by the Self and therefore they cannot guide the Self; they are dependent. Whatever is expressed is mortal, and whatever is not the Self is expressed.</span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;" class="MsoHyperlink"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">Excerpts from:</b></span></p>
<p><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: book antiqua,palatino;"> <b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="line-height: 115%;">Brahman -The Self <span class="MsoHyperlink">- </span>Mantras 4-8: Kenopanishad â€“ </span></b><span style="line-height: 115%;"><a href="http://www.swami-krishnananda.org/essay/essay_2.html"><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="line-height: 115%;">Essays on the Upanishads</span></b></a></span><b style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"> by Swami Krishnananda</span></b></span></p>
